# Task: Refactor Roslyn Symbol Lookup to Unified Resolution Strategy

## Background
Roslyn's symbol lookup has separate code paths for different contexts (expression binding, type resolution, member access). This task extracts common patterns into a shared strategy.

## Objective
Create a `UnifiedSymbolResolver` that consolidates the common symbol lookup patterns used across different binding contexts.

## Steps
1. Study symbol resolution in `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/`
2. Identify common patterns in `Binder.LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder`, `Binder_Lookup.cs`, and type resolution
3. Create `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs` with:
   - A strategy interface `ISymbolResolutionStrategy`
   - Concrete strategies for: TypeResolution, MemberAccess, NamespaceResolution
   - A `Resolve()` method that walks scope chains using the strategy
   - Results type that captures both found symbols and diagnostics
4. Create a test file in the test directory

## Key Reference Files
- `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder_Lookup.cs`
- `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder.cs`
- `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Symbols/` — symbol types

## Success Criteria
- UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs exists
- Defines ISymbolResolutionStrategy interface
- Has concrete strategy implementations
- Test file exists

    23→    /// A LookupResult can be ONE OF:
    24→    ///    empty - nothing found.
    25→    ///    a viable result - this kind of result prevents lookup into further scopes of lower priority.
    26→    ///                      Viable results should be without error; ambiguity is handled in the caller.
    27→    ///                      (Note that handling multiple "viable" results is not the same as in the VB compiler)
    28→    ///    a non-accessible result - this kind of result means that search continues into further scopes of lower priority for
    29→    ///                      a viable result. An error is attached with the inaccessibility errors. Non-accessible results take priority over
    30→    ///                      non-viable results.
    31→    ///    a non-viable result - a result that means that the search continues into further scopes of low

    22→    /// 
    23→    /// A LookupResult can be ONE OF:
    24→    ///    empty - nothing found.
    25→    ///    a viable result - this kind of result prevents lookup into further scopes of lower priority.
    26→    ///                      Viable results should be without error; ambiguity is handled in the caller.
    27→    ///                      (Note that handling multiple "viable" results is not the same as in the VB compiler)
    28→    ///    a non-accessible result - this kind of result means that search continues into further scopes of lower priority for
    29→    ///                      a viable result. An error is attached with the inaccessibility errors. Non-accessible results take priority over
    30→    ///                      non-viable results.
    31→    ///    a non-viable result - a result that means that the search continues into further scopes of low

    15→    /// <summary>
    16→    /// Classifies the different ways in which a found symbol might be incorrect.
    17→    /// Higher values are considered "better" than lower values. These values are used
    18→    /// in a few different places:
    19→    ///    1) Inside a LookupResult to indicate the quality of a symbol from lookup.
    20→    ///    2) Inside a bound node (for example, BoundBadExpression), to indicate
    21→    ///       the "binding quality" of the symbols referenced by that bound node.
    22→    ///    3) Inside an error type symbol, to indicate the reason that the candidate symbols
    23→    ///       in the error type symbols were not good.
    24→    ///       
    25→    /// While most of the values can occur in all places, some of the problems are not
    26→    /// detected at lookup time (e.g., NotAVariable), so only occur in bound nodes.

    28→    /// <remarks>

    33→    ///   1) CandidateReason in language-independent, while this enum

    11→namespace Microsoft.CodeAnalysis.CSharp
    12→{
    13→    /// <summary>
    14→    /// Represents a result of lookup operation over a 0 or 1 symbol (as opposed to a scope). The
    15→    /// typical use is to represent that a particular symbol is good/bad/unavailable.
    16→    /// 
    17→    /// For more explanation of Kind, Symbol, Error - see LookupResult.
    18→    /// </summary>
    19→    internal readonly struct SingleLookupResult
    20→    {
    21→        // the kind of result.
    22→        internal readonly LookupResultKind Kind;
    23→
    24→        // the symbol or null.
    25→        internal readonly Symbol Symbol;
    26→
    27→        // the error of the result, if it is NonViable or Inaccessible
    28→        internal readonly DiagnosticInfo Error;
    29→
    30→        internal SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind kind, Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)
    31→        {
    32→            this.Kind = kind;
    33→            this.Symbol = symbol;
    34→            this.Error = error;
    35→        }
    36→    }
    37→}

  1293→        internal static ImmutableArray<Symbol> GetCandidateMembers(NamespaceOrTypeSymbol nsOrType, string name, LookupOptions options, Binder originalBinder)
  1294→        {
  1295→            if ((options & LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly) != 0 && nsOrType is TypeSymbol)

    10→    /// A distinct scope that may expose extension methods. For a particular Binder,  there
    11→    /// are two possible scopes: one for the namespace, and another for any using statements
    12→    /// in the namespace. The namespace scope is searched before the using scope.
    13→    /// </summary>

    15→    {
    16→        public readonly Binder Binder;

    21→        }
    22→    }
    23→

    29→    {
    30→        private readonly Binder _binder;
    31→
    32→        public ExtensionMethodScopes(Binder binder)

  1724→        {
  1725→            // If a member is a method or event, or if it is a constant, field or property of 
  1726→            // either a delegate type or the type dynamic, then the member is said to be invocable.

## Summary: Roslyn Binder Symbol Lookup Patterns Analysis

Based on my thorough analysis of the Roslyn Binder class in `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/`, here's a comprehensive breakdown of the symbol lookup patterns:

---

### 1. KEY LOOKUP METHODS AND SIGNATURES

**Primary Lookup Entry Points:**

- **`LookupSymbolsInternal()`** (lines 81-113)
  - Walks through binder scope chain: `for (var scope = this; scope != null && !result.IsMultiViable; scope = scope.Next)`
  - Stops when finding viable results or reaching end of chain
  - Signature: `Binder LookupSymbolsInternal(LookupResult result, string name, int arity, ConsList<TypeSymbol> basesBeingResolved, LookupOptions options, bool diagnose, ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol> useSiteInfo)`

- **`LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder()`** (virtual at line 115-118)
  - Core override point for subclasses to implement scope-specific lookup
  - Base Binder implementation is empty; overridden in LocalScopeBinder, InContainerBinder, etc.
  - Signature: `virtual void LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder(LookupResult result, string name, int arity, ConsList<TypeSymbol> basesBeingResolved, LookupOptions options, Binder originalBinder, bool diagnose, ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol> useSiteInfo)`

- **`LookupSymbolsOrMembersInternal()`** (lines 125-143)
  - Dispatcher: handles both unqualified lookup and member lookup
  - Routes to either `LookupSymbolsInternal()` or `LookupMembersInternal()` based on `qualifierOpt`

- **`LookupMembersInternal()`** (lines 164-177)
  - Looks up members in a specific namespace or type
  - Routes to type-specific handlers: `LookupMembersInType()`, `LookupMembersInNamespace()`

Perfect! I've completed the planning phase and created a comprehensive implementation plan. Here's what I've designed:

## Implementation Plan Summary

**Objective**: Create a `UnifiedSymbolResolver` that consolidates common symbol lookup patterns used across different binding contexts.

### Key Components to Implement

1. **ISymbolResolutionStrategy Interface**
   - Defines contract for different resolution strategies
   - Core method: `Execute()` for strategy-specific lookup logic

2. **SymbolResolutionResults Type**
   - Captures resolution results (symbols, kind, errors)

3. **Four Concrete Strategies**:
   - `TypeResolutionStrategy` - For member lookup in types/namespaces
   - `UnqualifiedNameResolutionStrategy` - For scope chain walking
   - `ExtensionMethodResolutionStrategy` - For extension method lookup
   - `NamespaceResolutionStrategy` - For namespace hierarchy resolution

4. **UnifiedSymbolResolver Class**
   - Central orchestrator with `Resolve()` method
   - Handles scope iteration, result merging, and early exit optimization
   - Implements two-phase lookup (optimize by deferring diagnostics)

5. **Comprehensive Tests**
   - Test file: `UnifiedSymbolResolverTests.cs`
   - Coverage for all strategies
   - Integration tests for the resolver

### Design Highlights
- **Additive approach**: No modifications to existing `Binder.cs` or other files
- **Reuses existing infrastructure**: Leverages `LookupResult`, `LookupOptions`, existing helpers
- **Maintains compatibility**: Drop-in enhancement to existing lookup system
- **Well-tested**: Comprehensive test coverage using existing Roslyn test patterns

The plan is detailed in `/logs/agent/sessions/plans/curious-waddling-hellman.md`.

An error is attached with the inaccessibility errors. Non-accessible results take priority over\n    ///                      non-viable results.\n    ///    a non-viable result - a result that means that the search continues into further scopes of lower priority for\n    ///                          a viable or non-accessible result. An error is attached with the error that indicates\n    ///                          why the result is non-viable.  A typical reason would be that it is the wrong kind of symbol.\n    /// \n    /// Note that the class is poolable so its instances can be obtained from a pool via GetInstance.\n    /// Also it is a good idea to call Free on instances after they no longer needed.\n    /// \n    /// The typical pattern is \"caller allocates / caller frees\" -\n    ///    \n    ///    var result = LookupResult.GetInstance();\n    ///  \n    ///    scope.Lookup(result, \"goo\");\n    ///    ... use result ...\n    ///         \n    ///    result.Clear();\n    ///    anotherScope.Lookup(result, \"moo\");\n    ///    ... use result ...\n    /// \n    ///    result.Free();   //result and its content is invalid after this\n    ///    \n    /// \n    /// \n    /// </summary>\n    /// <remarks>\n    /// Currently LookupResult is intended only for name lookup, not for overload resolution. It is\n    /// not clear if overload resolution will work with the structure as is, require enhancements,\n    /// or be best served by an alternate mechanism.\n    /// \n    /// We might want to extend this to a more general priority scheme.\n    /// \n    /// </remarks>\n    internal sealed class LookupResult\n    {\n        // the kind of result.\n        private LookupResultKind _kind;\n\n        // If there is more than one symbol, they are stored in this list.\n        private readonly ArrayBuilder<Symbol> _symbolList;\n\n        // the error of the result, if it is NonViable or Inaccessible\n        private DiagnosticInfo _error;\n\n        private readonly ObjectPool<LookupResult> _pool;\n\n        private LookupResult(ObjectPool<LookupResult> pool)\n        {\n            _pool = pool;\n            _kind = LookupResultKind.Empty;\n            _symbolList = new ArrayBuilder<Symbol>();\n            _error = null;\n        }\n\n        internal bool IsClear\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return _kind == LookupResultKind.Empty && _error == null && _symbolList.Count == 0;\n            }\n        }\n\n        internal void Clear()\n        {\n            _kind = LookupResultKind.Empty;\n            _symbolList.Clear();\n            _error = null;\n        }\n\n        internal LookupResultKind Kind\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return _kind;\n            }\n        }\n\n        /// <summary>\n        /// Return the single symbol if there is exactly one, otherwise null.\n        /// </summary>\n        internal Symbol SingleSymbolOrDefault\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return (_symbolList.Count == 1) ? _symbolList[0] : null;\n            }\n        }\n\n        internal ArrayBuilder<Symbol> Symbols\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return _symbolList;\n            }\n        }\n\n        internal DiagnosticInfo Error\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return _error;\n            }\n        }\n\n        /// <summary>\n        /// Is the result viable with one or more symbols?\n        /// </summary>\n        internal bool IsMultiViable\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return Kind == LookupResultKind.Viable;\n            }\n        }\n\n        /// <summary>\n        /// NOTE: Even there is a single viable symbol, it may be an error type symbol.\n        /// </summary>\n        internal bool IsSingleViable\n        {\n            get\n            {\n                return Kind == LookupResultKind.Viable && _symbolList.Count == 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult Good(Symbol symbol)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.Viable, symbol, null);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult WrongArity(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.WrongArity, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult Empty()\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.Empty, null, null);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult NotReferencable(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.NotReferencable, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult StaticInstanceMismatch(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.StaticInstanceMismatch, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult Inaccessible(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.Inaccessible, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult NotInvocable(Symbol unwrappedSymbol, Symbol symbol, bool diagnose)\n        {\n            var diagInfo = diagnose ? new CSDiagnosticInfo(ErrorCode.ERR_NonInvocableMemberCalled, unwrappedSymbol) : null;\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.NotInvocable, symbol, diagInfo);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult NotLabel(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.NotLabel, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult NotTypeOrNamespace(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.NotATypeOrNamespace, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult NotTypeOrNamespace(Symbol unwrappedSymbol, Symbol symbol, bool diagnose)\n        {\n            // TODO: determine correct diagnosis \n            var diagInfo = diagnose ? new CSDiagnosticInfo(ErrorCode.ERR_BadSKknown, unwrappedSymbol.Name, unwrappedSymbol.GetKindText(), MessageID.IDS_SK_TYPE.Localize()) : null;\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.NotATypeOrNamespace, symbol, diagInfo);\n        }\n\n        internal static SingleLookupResult NotAnAttributeType(Symbol symbol, DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            return new SingleLookupResult(LookupResultKind.NotAnAttributeType, symbol, error);\n        }\n\n        /// <summary>\n        /// Set current result according to another.\n        /// </summary>\n        internal void SetFrom(SingleLookupResult other)\n        {\n            _kind = other.Kind;\n            _symbolList.Clear();\n            _symbolList.Add(other.Symbol);\n            _error = other.Error;\n        }\n\n        /// <summary>\n        /// Set current result according to another.\n        /// </summary>\n        internal void SetFrom(LookupResult other)\n        {\n            _kind = other._kind;\n            _symbolList.Clear();\n            _symbolList.AddRange(other._symbolList);\n            _error = other._error;\n        }\n\n        internal void SetFrom(DiagnosticInfo error)\n        {\n            this.Clear();\n            _error Mutates the current result.\n        internal void MergePrioritized(LookupResult other)\n        {\n            if (other.Kind > Kind)\n            {\n                SetFrom(other);\n            }\n        }\n\n        /// <summary>\n        /// Merge another result with this one, with the symbols combined if both\n        /// this and other are viable. Otherwise the highest priority result wins (this if equal \n        /// priority and non-viable.)\n        /// </summary>\n        internal void MergeEqual(LookupResult other)\n        {\n            if (Kind > other.Kind)\n            {\n                return;\n            }\n            else if (other.Kind > Kind)\n            {\n                this.SetFrom(other);\n            }\n            else if (Kind != LookupResultKind.Viable)\n            {\n                // this makes the operator not symmetrical, but so far we do not care.\n                // it is really a matter of which error gets reported.\n                return;\n            }\n            else\n            {\n                // Merging two viable results together. We will always end up with at least two symbols.\n                _symbolList.AddRange(other._symbolList);\n            }\n        }\n\n        internal void MergeEqual(SingleLookupResult result)\n        {\n            if (Kind > result.Kind)\n            {\n                // existing result is better\n            }\n            else if (result.Kind > Kind)\n            {\n                this.SetFrom(result);\n            }\n            else if ((object)result.Symbol != null)\n            {\n                // Same goodness. Include all symbols\n                _symbolList.Add(result.Symbol);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // global pool\n        //TODO: consider if global pool is ok.\n        private static readonly ObjectPool<LookupResult> s_poolInstance = CreatePool();\n\n        // if someone needs to create a pool\n        internal static ObjectPool<LookupResult> CreatePool()\n        {\n            ObjectPool<LookupResult> pool = null;\n            pool = new ObjectPool<LookupResult>(() => new LookupResult(pool), 128); // we rarely need more than 10\n            return pool;\n        }\n\n        internal static LookupResult GetInstance()\n        {\n            var instance = s_poolInstance.Allocate();\n            Debug.Assert(instance.IsClear);\n            return instance;\n        }\n\n        internal void Free()\n        {\n            this.Clear();\n            if (_pool != null)\n            {\n                _pool.Free(this);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n",

SCOPE WALKING PATTERNS\n\n**Scope Chain Walking:**\n\nThe Binder class uses a linked-list pattern where each Binder has a `Next` property:\n\n```\nBinder.Next -> Binder.Next -> Binder.Next -> ... -> BuckStopsHereBinder (null)\n```\n\n**Pattern in `LookupSymbolsInternal()` (lines 88-111):**\n\n```csharp\nBinder binder = null;\nfor (var scope = this; scope != null && !result.IsMultiViable; scope = scope.Next)\n{\n    if (binder != null)\n    {\n        var tmp = LookupResult.GetInstance();\n        scope.LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder(tmp, ...);\n        result.MergeEqual(tmp);      // Merge with higher-priority results\n        tmp.Free();\n    }\n    else\n    {\n        scope.LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder(result, ...);\n        if (!result.IsClear)\n        {\n            binder = scope;           // Track first non-empty scope\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if ((options & LookupOptions.LabelsOnly) != 0 && scope.IsLastBinderWithinMember())\n    {\n        break;  // Labels don't cross member boundaries\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Key Points:**\n- Early exit when `IsMultiViable` is found\n- Different handling for first scope vs. subsequent scopes (pooled temp results)\n- Special handling for label lookups (stops at member boundary)\n\n**Hierarchy Walking in Classes (lines 812-857):**\n\n```csharp\nTypeSymbol currentType = type;\nwhile ((object)currentType != null)\n{\n    LookupMembersWithoutInheritance(tmp, currentType, ...);\n    MergeHidingLookupResults(result, tmp, ...);  // Apply hiding rules\n    \n    // Check if we can stop early\n    if (result.IsMultiViable && (tmpHidesMethodOrIndexers || !IsMethodOrIndexer(result.Symbols[0])))\n    {\n        break;\n    }\n    \n    // Move to next base type\n    currentType = currentType.GetNextBaseTypeNoUseSiteDiagnostics(basesBeingResolved, ...);\n}\n```\n\n**Interface Walking (lines 1136-1144):**\n\n```csharp\nforeach (NamedTypeSymbol baseInterface in interfaces)\n{\n    if (seenInterfaces is null || seenInterfaces.Add(baseInterface))\n    {\n        LookupMembersWithoutInheritance(tmp, baseInterface, ...);\n        MergeHidingLookupResults(current, tmp, ...);\n        tmp.Clear();\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. LOOKUP RESULT STRUCTURE AND MERGING\n\n**`LookupResult` Class** (LookupResult.cs, lines 14-323):\n\nKey fields and properties:\n- `LookupResultKind _kind` - Indicates quality of result (see below)\n- `ArrayBuilder<Symbol> _symbolList` - May contain multiple symbols\n- `DiagnosticInfo _error` - Error info for non-viable results\n- `IsClear` - True if empty with no error\n- `SingleSymbolOrDefault` - Returns single symbol or null\n- `IsMultiViable` - True if kind == Viable with one or more symbols\n\n**Result Priority Hierarchy** (LookupResultKind.cs, lines 38-67):\n\nOrdered from lowest to highest priority:\n```\nEmpty < NotATypeOrNamespace < NotAnAttributeType < WrongArity < \nNotCreatable < Inaccessible < NotReferencable < NotAValue < \nNotAVariable < NotInvocable < NotLabel < StaticInstanceMismatch < \nOverloadResolutionFailure < Ambiguous < MemberGroup < Viable\n```\n\n**Merging Strategies:**\n\n1. **`MergeEqual(LookupResult other)`** (lines 256-277)\n   - Used when scopes have equal priority\n   - If both viable: combines symbols\n   - Otherwise: highest priority wins, \"this\" wins on ties\n\n2. **`MergePrioritized(LookupResult other)`** (lines 243-249)\n   - Used across different priority levels\n   - If `other.Kind > this.Kind`: takes entire result from `other`\n\n3. **`MergeHidingLookupResults()`** (lines 1224-1278)\n   - Applied between inheritance levels\n   - Non-methods hide everything\n   - Methods hide non-methods\n   - Methods of same name don't hide each other (handled later in overload resolution)\n   - Checks inheritance relationships to determine if hiding applies\n\n---\n\n### 4. LOOKUP OPTIONS AND THEIR USAGE\n\n**Option Flags** (LookupOptions.cs, lines 21-113):\n\n| Flag | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `NamespaceAliasesOnly` | Only alias symbols |\n| `NamespacesOrTypesOnly` | Filter for types/namespaces |\n| `MustBeInvocableIfMember` | Only if method/event or delegate-type field/property |\n| `MustBeInstance` | Instance members only |\n| `MustNotBeInstance` | Static members only |\n| `MustNotBeNamespace` | Exclude namespaces |\n| `AllMethodsOnArityZero` | Consider generic methods even if arity=0 |\n| `LabelsOnly` | Label lookup only (exclusive) |\n| `UseBaseReferenceAccessibility` | Use base.X accessibility rules |\n| `IncludeExtensionMethods` | Include extension methods |\n| `AttributeTypeOnly` | Attribute type lookup (with \"Attribute\" suffix) |\n| `VerbatimNameAttributeTypeOnly` | Attribute lookup without suffix |\n| `AllNamedTypesOnArityZero` | Consider generic types even if arity=0 |\n| `MustNotBeMethodTypeParameter` | Exclude method type parameters |\n| `MustBeAbstractOrVirtual` | Abstract or virtual only |\n| `MustNotBeParameter` | Exclude parameters |\n\n**Option Filtering in `CheckViability()`** (lines 1385-1538):\n\nEarly filters apply options to validate symbols:\n\n```csharp\n// Accessibility wrapper\nif ((options & LookupOptions.MustNotBeParameter) != 0 && unwrappedSymbol is ParameterSymbol)\n    return LookupResult.Empty();\n\n// Type filtering\nif ((options & LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly) != 0 && !(unwrappedSymbol is NamespaceOrTypeSymbol))\n    return LookupResult.NotTypeOrNamespace(...);\n\n// Instance/Static filtering\nif ((options & LookupOptions.MustBeInstance) != 0 && !IsInstance(unwrappedSymbol))\n    return LookupResult.StaticInstanceMismatch(...);\n\nif ((options & LookupOptions.MustNotBeInstance) != 0 && IsInstance(unwrappedSymbol))\n    return LookupResult.StaticInstanceMismatch(...);\n\n// Label-specific\nif ((options & LookupOptions.LabelsOnly) != 0 && unwrappedSymbol.Kind != SymbolKind.Label)\n    return LookupResult.NotLabel(...);\n```\n\n**Helper Extension Methods** (lines 178-206):\n\n- `CanConsiderMembers()` - True if not restricted by namespace/label options\n- `CanConsiderLocals()` - True if not restricted by namespace/label options\n- `CanConsiderTypes()` - Excludes NamespaceAliasesOnly, MustBeInvocableIfMember, etc.\n- `CanConsiderNamespaces()` - Excludes MustNotBeNamespace, MustBeInstance, etc.\n\n---\n\n### 5. DIFFERENT LOOKUP CONTEXTS\n\n**Unqualified Name Lookup:**\n- Entry: `LookupSymbolsInternal()` - walks scope chain\n- Searches locals, labels, type/namespace members, aliases\n- Used in expression binding: `identifier`, `method()`, etc.\n\n**Qualified Member Access:**\n- Entry: `LookupMembersInternal()` with a specific `qualifierOpt` type/namespace\n- No scope chain walking\n- Walks type hierarchy (base classes/interfaces)\n- Used in: `obj.Member`, `Type.Member`, `ns.Type`, etc.\n\n**Extension Method Lookup:**\n- Entry: `LookupExtensionMethods()` with scope enumerator\n- Searches namespace scopes in order\n- Stops at first applicable method group\n- Used when: no suitable instance/static member found\n\n**Type Resolution Context:**\n- Walks namespace hierarchy\n- Respects using directives and aliases\n- Used in: `using X;`, base class declarations, field/parameter types\n\n**Attribute Type Lookup:**\n- Special: tries name first, then name+\"Attribute\"\n- Used in: `[Attribute]` syntax\n- Respects `VerbatimNameAttributeTypeOnly` option to suppress suffix lookup\n\n**Label Lookup:**\n- Scope: limited to current member\n- Options: `LabelsOnly` (exclusive flag)\n- Stops at `IsLastBinderWithinMember()`\n\n**Submission Lookup (REPL):**\n- Special handling via `LookupMembersInSubmissions()` (lines 255-371)\n- Two-phase search:\n  1. Find first match\n  2. If it's overloadable (method/indexer), collect all overloads across submission chain\n  3. Stop if non-overloadable member found\n\n---\n\n### 6. CONCRETE IMPLEMENTATION EXAMPLES\n\n**LocalScopeBinder (LocalScopeBinder.cs, lines 421-460):**\n\n```csharp\ninternal override void LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder(\n    LookupResult result, string name, int arity, ConsList<TypeSymbol> basesBeingResolved, \n    LookupOptions options, Binder originalBinder, bool diagnose, \n    ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol> useSiteInfo)\n{\n    // Label lookup\n    if ((options & LookupOptions.LabelsOnly) != 0)\n    {\n        var labelsMap = this.LabelsMap;\n        if (labelsMap != null && labelsMap.TryGetValue(name, out var labelSymbol))\n            result.MergeEqual(LookupResult.Good(labelSymbol));\n        return;\n    }\n\n    // Local variable lookup\n    var localsMap = this.LocalsMap;\n    if (localsMap != null && (options & LookupOptions.NamespaceAliasesOnly) == 0)\n    {\n        if (localsMap.TryGetValue(name, out var localSymbol))\n            result.MergeEqual(originalBinder.CheckViability(localSymbol, arity, options, null, diagnose, ref useSiteInfo, basesBeingResolved));\n    }\n\n    // Local function lookup\n    var localFunctionsMap = this.LocalFunctionsMap;\n    if (localFunctionsMap != null && options.CanConsiderLocals())\n    {\n        if (localFunctionsMap.TryGetValue(name, out var localSymbol))\n            result.MergeEqual(originalBinder.CheckViability(localSymbol, arity, options, null, diagnose, ref useSiteInfo, basesBeingResolved));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**InContainerBinder (InContainerBinder.cs, lines 103-129):**\n\n```csharp\ninternal override void LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder(\n    LookupResult result, string name, int arity, ConsList<TypeSymbol> basesBeingResolved, \n    LookupOptions options, Binder originalBinder, bool diagnose, \n    ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol> useSiteInfo)\n{\n    // First lookup members of the container (namespace or type)\n    if ((options & LookupOptions.NamespaceAliasesOnly) == 0)\n    {\n        this.LookupMembersInternal(result, _container, name, arity, basesBeingResolved, options, originalBinder, diagnose, ref useSiteInfo);\n\n        if (result.IsMultiViable)\n        {\n            // withUsingAliases.IsUsingAlias(name, originalBinder.IsSemanticModelBinder, basesBeingResolved))\n                {\n                    // Report error and return error symbol\n                    var result.MergeEqual(resultOfThisMember);\n    }\n\n    methods.Free();\n}\n```\n\n**GetCandidateMembers() (lines 1293-1315):**\n\n```csharp\ninternal static ImmutableArray<Symbol> GetCandidateMembers(\n    NamespaceOrTypeSymbol nsOrType, string name, LookupOptions options, Binder originalBinder)\n{\n    // Filter for types only\n    if ((options & LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly) != 0 && nsOrType is TypeSymbol)\n        return nsOrType.GetTypeMembers(name).Cast<NamedTypeSymbol, Symbol>();\n\n    // Early attribute binding mode\n    if (nsOrType.Kind == SymbolKind.NamedType && originalBinder.IsEarlyAttributeBinder)\n        return ((NamedTypeSymbol)nsOrType).GetEarlyAttributeDecodingMembers(name);\n\n    // Labels don't have members\n    if ((options & LookupOptions.LabelsOnly) != 0)\n        return ImmutableArray<Symbol>.Empty;\n\n    // Primary constructor special case\n    if (nsOrType is SourceMemberContainerTypeSymbol { HasPrimaryConstructor: true } sourceMemberContainerTypeSymbol)\n        return sourceMemberContainerTypeSymbol.GetCandidateMembersForLookup(name);\n\n    // Standard member lookup\n    return nsOrType.GetMembers(name);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### FILE REFERENCES\n\n- **Main Lookup Implementation:** `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder_Lookup.cs` (2050 lines)\n- **Result An error is attached with the inaccessibility errors. Non-accessible results take priority over\n    30\u2192    ///                      non-viable results.\n    31\u2192    ///    a non-viable result - a result that means that the search continues into further scopes of lower priority for\n    32\u2192    ///                          a viable or non-accessible result. An error is attached with the error that indicates\n    33\u2192    ///                          why the result is non-viable.  A typical reason would be that it is the wrong kind of symbol.\n    34\u2192    /// \n    35\u2192    /// Note that the class is poolable so its instances can be obtained from a pool via GetInstance.\n    36\u2192    /// Also it is a good idea to call Free on instances after they no longer needed.\n    37\u2192    /// \n    38\u2192    /// The typical pattern is \"caller allocates / caller frees\" -\n    39\u2192    ///    \n    40\u2192    ///    var result = LookupResult.GetInstance();\n    41\u2192    ///  \n    42\u2192    ///    scope.Lookup(result, \"goo\");\n    43\u2192    ///    ... use result ...\n    44\u2192    ///         \n    45\u2192    ///    result.Clear();\n    46\u2192    ///    anotherScope.Lookup(result, \"moo\");\n    47\u2192    ///    ... use result ...\n    48\u2192    /// \n    49\u2192    ///    result.Free();   //result and its content is invalid after this\n    50\u2192    ///    \n    51\u2192    /// \n    52\u2192    /// \n    53\u2192    /// </summary>\n    54\u2192    /// <remarks>\n    55\u2192    /// Currently LookupResult is intended only for name lookup, not for overload resolution. It is\n    56\u2192    /// not clear if overload resolution will work with the structure as is, require enhancements,\n    57\u2192    /// or be best served by an alternate mechanism.\n    58\u2192    /// \n    59\u2192    /// We might want to extend this to a more general priority scheme.\n    60\u2192    /// \n    61\u2192    /// </remarks>\n    62\u2192    internal sealed class LookupResult\n    63\u2192    {\n    64\u2192        // the kind of result.\n    65\u2192        private LookupResultKind _kind;\n    66\u2192\n    67\u2192        // If there is more than one symbol, they are stored in this list.\n    68\u2192        private readonly ArrayBuilder<Symbol> _symbolList;\n    69\u2192\n    70\u2192        // the error of the result, if it is NonViable or Inaccessible\n    71\u2192        private DiagnosticInfo _error;\n    72\u2192\n    73\u2192        private readonly ObjectPool<LookupResult> _pool;\n    74\u2192\n    75\u2192        private LookupResult(ObjectPool<LookupResult> pool)\n    76\u2192        {\n    77\u2192            _pool = pool;\n    78\u2192            _kind = LookupResultKind.Empty;\n    79\u2192            _symbolList = new ArrayBuilder<Symbol>();\n    80\u2192            _error = null;\n    81\u2192        }\n    82\u2192\n    83\u2192        internal bool IsClear\n    84\u2192        {\n    85\u2192            get\n    86\u2192            {\n    87\u2192                return _kind == LookupResultKind.Empty && _error == null && _symbolList.Count == 0;\n    88\u2192            }\n    89\u2192        }\n    90\u2192\n    91\u2192        internal void Clear()\n    92\u2192        {\n    93\u2192            _kind = LookupResultKind.Empty;\n    94\u2192            _symbolList.Clear();\n    95\u2192            _error = null;\n _kind;\n   103\u2192            }\n   104\u2192        }\n   105\u2192\n   106\u2192        /// <summary>\n   107\u2192        /// Return the single symbol if there is exactly one, otherwise null.\n   108\u2192        /// </summary>\n   109\u2192        internal Symbol SingleSymbolOrDefault\n   110\u2192        {\n   111\u2192            get\n   112\u2192            {\n   113\u2192 {\n   119\u2192            get\n   120\u2192            {\n   121\u2192                return _symbolList;\n   122\u2192            }\n   123\u2192        }\n   124\u2192\n   125\u2192        internal   "content": "# UnifiedSymbolResolver Implementation Plan\n\n## Context\nRoslyn's symbol lookup has multiple separate code paths for different contexts (unqualified name lookup, member access, extension methods) that share common patterns but lack a unified abstraction. This refactoring extracts these patterns into a reusable strategy-based approach, improving maintainability and reducing duplication.\n\n## Key Findings from Analysis\n\n### Common Patterns Identified\n1. **Scope Walking**: All lookups iterate through scope chain via `Binder.Next` until finding viable results\n2. **Result Merging**: Use `LookupResult.MergeEqual()` to combine results from different scopes\n3. **Viability Checking**: Apply `CheckViability()` to filter results by `LookupOptions`\n4. **Two-phase Lookup**: Optimize by first attempting without diagnostics, retrying with diagnostics only if needed\n5. **Early Exit**: Stop iteration when `IsMultiViable` result found\n\n### Different Resolution Contexts\n- **Unqualified Name Lookup** (`LookupSymbolsInternal`): Walk scope chain, search locals/labels/members\n- **Member Access** (`LookupMembersInternal`): Walk type hierarchy, apply hiding rules\n- **Extension Methods** (`LookupExtensionMethods`): Iterate through namespace scopes\n- **Namespace Resolution**: Walk namespace hierarchy respecting using directives\n- **Type Resolution**: Resolve types in hierarchies and constraint contexts\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\n### 1. Core Components\n\n**File**: `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs`\n\n#### 1.1 ISymbolResolutionStrategy Interface\n```\nPurpose: Define contract for different resolution strategies\nMethods:\n  - void Execute(Binder scope, LookupResult result, ...)\n  - bool ShouldContinueSearch(LookupResult current)\n```\n\n#### 1.2 SymbolResolutionResults Type\n```\nPurpose: Capture resolution results (found symbols + diagnostics)\nFields:\n  - ImmutableArray<Symbol> Symbols\n  - LookupResultKind Kind\n  - DiagnosticInfo Error\n  - bool IsViable\n```\n\n#### 1.3 Concrete Strategy Implementations\n\n**TypeResolutionStrategy**\n- Handles type/namespace member lookup\n- Routes based on `TypeKind` (Class, Interface, TypeParameter, etc.)\n- Applies inheritance hierarchy walking\n- Applies hiding rules between inheritance levels\n- Reference: `Binder.LookupMembersInternal()` lines 164-177\n\n**UnqualifiedNameResolutionStrategy**\n- Walks scope chain (local->container->using aliases->imports)\n- Handles labels, locals, type members\n- Applies options filtering\n- Reference: `Binder.LookupSymbolsInternal()` lines 81-113\n\n**ExtensionMethodResolutionStrategy**\n- Iterates through namespace scopes\n- Gets extension methods via `GetCandidateExtensionMethods()`\n- Filters by arity and options\n- Reference: `Binder.LookupExtensionMethods()` lines 47-53\n\n**NamespaceResolutionStrategy**\n- Walks namespace hierarchy\n- Respects using directives and aliases\n- Handles \"Attribute\" suffix for attribute types\n\n#### 1.4 UnifiedSymbolResolver Class\n```\nPurpose: Central resolver coordinating strategy selection and execution\nMethods:\n  - Resolve(ISymbolResolutionStrategy strategy, ...) -> SymbolResolutionResults\n  - ResolveWithFallback(strategy, ...) -> SymbolResolutionResults\n```\n\nKey Logic:\n- Orchestrates strategy execution\n- Implements two-phase lookup optimization (diagnose: false first, then true)\n- Handles scope chain iteration\n- Applies result merging\n- Provides early exit optimization\n\n### 2. Implementation Approach\n\n#### Phase 1: Create Base Infrastructure\n1. Define `ISymbolResolutionStrategy` interface\n2. Define `SymbolResolutionResults` record/struct\n3. Create `UnifiedSymbolResolver` base class with common logic\n\n#### Phase 2: Implement Strategies\n1. Implement `TypeResolutionStrategy` (most complex - involves hiding rules)\n2. Implement `UnqualifiedNameResolutionStrategy`\n3. Implement `ExtensionMethodResolutionStrategy`\n4. Implement `NamespaceResolutionStrategy`\n\n#### Phase 3: Integration (Future Work)\n- Refactor `Binder.LookupMembersInternal()` to use `TypeResolutionStrategy`\n- Refactor `Binder.LookupSymbolsInternal()` to use `UnqualifiedNameResolutionStrategy`\n- Update `Binder.LookupExtensionMethods()` to use `ExtensionMethodResolutionStrategy`\n\n### 3. Design Constraints\n\n**Keep It Focused**:\n- Do NOT refactor existing methods - they continue to work as-is\n- Do NOT change method signatures\n- Do NOT modify `Binder.cs` itself\n- Do NOT add dependencies beyond what Binder already uses\n\n**Leverage Existing Infrastructure**:\n- Reuse existing `LookupResult`, `LookupOptions`, `SingleLookupResult`\n- Reuse existing helper methods: `CheckViability()`, `GetCandidateMembers()`\n- Reuse existing scope walking patterns from `Binder`\n\n**Architecture**:\n- Strategy interface is internal (not public API)\n- Resolver is utility/helper class, not part of core Binder chain\n- No circular dependencies\n- Compatible with existing binder architecture\n\n## File Locations and Critical References\n\n**New File to Create**:\n- `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs`\n\n**Reference Implementations**:\n- `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder_Lookup.cs` - Lines 81-113 (unqualified), 164-177 (member), 47-53 (extension)\n- `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/LookupResult.cs` - Result structure and merging\n- `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/LookupOptions.cs` - Option filtering\n- `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder.cs` - Core Binder class\n\n**Test File to Create**:\n- `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Test/Semantic/Semantics/UnifiedSymbolResolverTests.cs`\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n**Test Coverage**:\n1. TypeResolutionStrategy\n   - Class member lookup\n   - Interface member lookup\n   - Type parameter constraint lookup\n   - Hiding rules (non-methods hide everything)\n\n2. UnqualifiedNameResolutionStrategy\n   - Local variable lookup\n   - Label lookup\n   - Type member lookup\n   - Scope chain termination\n\n3. ExtensionMethodResolutionStrategy\n   - Single scope extension method lookup\n   - Namespace scope iteration\n   - Arity filtering\n\n4. # Roslyn Symbol Lookup Refactoring

## Project: UnifiedSymbolResolver

### Key Understanding
- Symbol lookup in Roslyn has multiple code paths: LookupSymbolsInternal, LookupMembersInternal, LookupExtensionMethods
- Common pattern: Walk through scope chain (Binder.Next), lookup in each scope, merge results using LookupResult
- LookupResult tracks: kind (Viable/NonViable/Inaccessible), symbols (ArrayBuilder), error info
- Different contexts (type resolution, member access, namespace resolution) all follow similar patterns

### File Structure
- Main lookup logic: `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder_Lookup.cs` (~2050 lines)
- Core binder: `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder.cs` (~39KB)
- Lookup types: `LookupResult.cs`, `LookupResultKind.cs`, `LookupOptions.cs`
- Symbol types: `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Symbols/`
- Existing tests: `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Test/Semantic/Semantics/LookupTests.cs`

### Common Lookup Patterns
1. **Scope Walking**: Iterate through Binder chain via `scope.Next`
2. **Result Merging**: Use `LookupResult.MergeEqual()` or `MergePrioritized()`
3. **Diagnostics**: Two-phase lookup (no-diagnose, then diagnose if needed)
4. **Context Options**: `LookupOptions` enum controls behavior (AttributeTypeOnly, LabelsOnly, etc.)

# UnifiedSymbolResolver Implementation Plan

## Context
Roslyn's symbol lookup has multiple separate code paths for different contexts (unqualified name lookup, member access, extension methods) that share common patterns but lack a unified abstraction. This refactoring extracts these patterns into a reusable strategy-based approach, improving maintainability and reducing duplication.

## Key Findings from Analysis

### Common Patterns Identified
1. **Scope Walking**: All lookups iterate through scope chain via `Binder.Next` until finding viable results
2. **Result Merging**: Use `LookupResult.MergeEqual()` to combine results from different scopes
3. **Viability Checking**: Apply `CheckViability()` to filter results by `LookupOptions`
4. **Two-phase Lookup**: Optimize by first attempting without diagnostics, retrying with diagnostics only if needed
5. **Early Exit**: Stop iteration when `IsMultiViable` result found

### Different Resolution Contexts
- **Unqualified Name Lookup** (`LookupSymbolsInternal`): Walk scope chain, search locals/labels/members
- **Member Access** (`LookupMembersInternal`): Walk type hierarchy, apply hiding rules
- **Extension Methods** (`LookupExtensionMethods`): Iterate through namespace scopes
- **Namespace Resolution**: Walk namespace hierarchy respecting using directives
- **Type Resolution**: Resolve types in hierarchies and constraint contexts

## Implementation Strategy

### 1. Core Components

**File**: `/workspace/src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs`

#### 1.1 ISymbolResolutionStrategy Interface
```
Purpose: Define contract for different resolution strategies
Methods:
  - void Execute(Binder scope, LookupResult result, ...)
  - bool ShouldContinueSearch(LookupResult current)
```
